msg:I stayed here for two nights for a meeting. The location of the hotel is quite out of the way, and there is no place to eat outside. The hotel looks tall and grand from the outside, but the space inside feels cramped and long and narrow.
Compared with the room fee of nearly 800, there are many flaws:

- Check in was relatively early, and the front desk still gave a non-river view room. I only remembered when I opened the door. Forget it, I forgot to ask. Because I have developed a habit of leaving billing information when checking in for business trips, so that I can leave quickly when I check out. As a result, when I left, the front desk said I was sorry and it hadnâ€™t opened yet. This is the first time I have encountered such a situation in countless five-star hotels in China. Many people forget that the reason is very far-fetched. This hotel is with the conference center, and it is usually full for meetings. Since there is such a premise, there should be a plan, not to mention that other hotels are full of rooms during peak seasons.
-The bathroom is rather narrow. The hair dryer doesn't work well, it burns your head when the wind is strong, the temperature is lowered and the wind is very weak, it should be very cheap, not worthy of the price. There are many choices for breakfast but the taste is average.
- The whole hotel feels more Chinese style, there are no knives and forks, only chopsticks, and the coffee is not good.
-Twice left the table for breakfast to get things back and the table was cleared despite coats on the chairs, key cards on the table, face masks and undrinked coffee and half-eaten plates. Although I appreciate this spirit of active service, you need to use your brain when doing things
d
In short, I feel that this kind of state-owned hotel still has a lot of deficiencies in management. I can feel that the staff are working hard to provide services, but the management of many details is not enough. If it is not specified for a business trip, he will definitely not come to live. Of course, his target audience may not be tourists.
